## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor concentration dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard form of rate laws in chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are ODE rate-law closures where reaction rate depends on concentration order, time-varying rate coefficients, or relaxation toward equilibrium.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate formation or depletion independent of A)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (linear dependence; sign of c0 sets growth vs decay)
- Pseudo-first-order with offset (source/sink): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (background generation plus first-order loss)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or autoconsumption approximations)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1; c0 < 0 gives stable relaxation)
- Autocatalytic (quadratic) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-acceleration with saturation/limited reagent)
- Time-dependent rate constant (exponential drift): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (temperature/catalyst activity drifting in time)
- Induction/activation factor on first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) * A (rate turns on after an induction period)
- Decaying catalyst/activity (deactivation): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A**c2 (combined time-dependence and non-integer order)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., modulated light or feed): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (oscillatory source term superposed on kinetic decay/growth)
- Nonlinear inhibition via rational damping: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate decreases at high A due to inhibition/transport limits)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Straight-line dA_dt vs A indicates linear (first-order) kinetics; slope gives the effective rate constant sign/magnitude.
- A stable equilibrium concentration shows up as dA_dt crossing zero at A = c1 with approximately linear behavior near that point: dA_dt ∝ (A - c1).
- Strong curvature in dA_dt vs A (especially steeper at larger A) suggests higher-order kinetics like A**2 or A**n with n > 1.
- An initial lag where dA_dt ≈ 0 for small t followed by faster change suggests an induction factor such as (1 - exp(c*t)) multiplying the A-dependent term.
- If the apparent rate accelerates or slows over time at fixed A, include explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient, commonly exp(c*t) or low-order polynomials in t.
- S-shaped time courses in A often correspond to autocatalytic structures dA_dt ∝ A*(c1 - A) rather than simple first/second order decay.
- If dA_dt magnitude saturates as A increases (sublinear response), rational damping forms like A/(1 + c*A) are indicative of inhibition or transport limitation.
- Periodic fluctuations in dA_dt at roughly constant amplitude/period point to sinusoidal forcing terms in t (e.g., light modulation, cycling conditions).

GT: -c0*A + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidate formulas: 55

GT is the fixed function of \(A\):
\[
f(A)= -0.23236613283613416\,A \;+\; 0.395876449251558\,\sin(0.5265654762365851\,A),
\]
i.e. “linear in \(A\) + a single sine with zero phase shift, and no constant offset, no \(A^2\), no \(t\) dependence”.

A candidate can match if we can set its free constants so that:
- all extra terms vanish (coefficients set to 0),
- the remaining linear coefficient equals \(-0.23236613283613416\),
- the remaining sine amplitude equals \(0.395876449251558\),
- the sine argument equals \(0.5265654762365851\,A\) (phase shift must be 0 mod \(2\pi\)),
- any absolute value can be removed by assuming the plausible domain \(A\ge 0\).

---

### 1. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Set \(c0=0\). Combine linear terms: need \(c1+c2=-0.23236613283613416\). Sine: set \(c3=0.395876449251558\), \(c4=0.5265654762365851\), \(c5=0\) (or \(2\pi k\)). Matches.

### 2. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)^2 + c4\)
Has \(\sin^2\), which cannot equal a pure \(\sin\) term for all \(A\) unless its coefficient is 0. If \(c1=0\), expression becomes linear+constant; GT has a sine term. No match.

### 3. \(Ac0 + c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Set \(c1=0\). Set \(c0=-0.23236613283613416\). Set \(c2=0.395876449251558\), \(c3=0.5265654762365851\), \(c4=0\) (or \(2\pi k\)). Matches.

### 4. \(Ac0 + c1 + c2\sin(c3|A|+c4)\)
Assume \(A\ge 0\) so \(|A|=A\). Then same as (3): set \(c1=0\), \(c0=-0.23236613283613416\), \(c2=0.395876449251558\), \(c3=0.5265654762365851\), \(c4=0\). Matches (conditional on \(A\ge0\)).

### 5. \(Ac0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6\)
Set \(c6=0\). Need \(c0+c1+c2=-0.23236613283613416\). Sine as in (1): \(c3=0.395876449251558\), \(c4=0.5265654762365851\), \(c5=0\). Matches.

### 6. \(Ac0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3\sin(c4|A|+c5)\)
Assume \(A\ge0\). Set \(c2=0\). Need \(c0+c1=-0.23236613283613416\). Set \(c3=0.395876449251558\), \(c4=0.5265654762365851\), \(c5=0\). Matches.

### 7. \(A^{c0}c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4) + c5\)
To get a linear term, set \(c0=1\) so \(A^{c0}c1=c1A\). Set \(c5=0\). Then choose \(c1=-0.23236613283613416\), \(c2=0.395876449251558\), \(c3=0.5265654762365851\), \(c4=0\). Matches.

### 8. \(Ac0 + Ac1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Need \(c0+c1=-0.23236613283613416\). Sine: \(c2=0.395876449251558\), \(c3=0.5265654762365851\), \(c4=0\). Matches.

### 9. \(Ac0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Need \(c0+c1+c2=-0.23236613283613416\). Sine: \(c3=0.395876449251558\), \(c4=0.5265654762365851\), \(c5=0\). Matches.

### 10. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)\)
Directly the GT form (no constant). Set \(c0=-0.23236613283613416\), \(c1=0.395876449251558\), \(c2=0.5265654762365851\), \(c3=0\) (or \(2\pi k\)). Matches.

### 11. \(A^{c0}c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
As in (7) but without constant: set \(c0=1\), \(c1=-0.23236613283613416\), \(c2=0.395876449251558\), \(c3=0.5265654762365851\), \(c4=0\). Matches.

### 12. \(A^3c0 + A^3c1 + Ac2 + Ac3 + Ac4 + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\)
Set \(c0=c1=0\). Need \(c2+c3+c4=-0.23236613283613416\). Sine: \(c5=0.395876449251558\), \(c6=0.5265654762365851\), \(c7=0\). Matches.

### 13. \(A^2c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c4 + c5\sin(Ac6+c7) + c8 e^{c9 t}\) (plus another \(A^2c1\) term shown)
Contains \(t\)-dependence unless those coefficients are zero or exponents force constants. Easiest: set all \(t\)-dependent parts to zero: set coefficient of \(A\exp(c3 t)\) term to 0 (its multiplier \(c2=0\) in the given structure is ambiguous, but you can set that whole coefficient to 0), and set \(c8=0\). Also set both \(A^2\) coefficients \(c0=c1=0\). Then reduce to \(A c4 + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\) and match by choosing \(c4=-0.23236613283613416\), \(c5=0.395876449251558\), \(c6=0.5265654762365851\), \(c7=0\). Matches.

### 14–17. Rational forms with \((A+c1)\) denominators and mixed sine/linear terms
To match GT (which has no denominator), we must eliminate the denominator effect. The only way for \(\frac{\text{poly}(A)}{A+c1}\) to become a polynomial for all \(A\) is if the numerator is divisible by \(A+c1\), which would generally introduce constants and/or higher powers not present, and still leaves extra structure. You can also try setting all denominator-bearing coefficients to 0, but then you lose needed linear/sine terms unless there is a free non-denominator sine term (only #17 has \(c6\sin(\cdot)\) outside).  
- **14,15,16**: all sine terms are tied to \((A+c1)\) denominators; if you zero them you can’t reproduce the sine. No match.  
- **17**: has \(c6\sin(Ac3+c4)\) outside, good; but the remaining non-sine part is \(A^2c0/(A+c1)+A c5/(A+c1)\). To equal \(-kA\) for all \(A\), this rational part must simplify to linear with no constant; generically it produces a constant term unless \(c1=0\), but \(c1=0\) makes it \(A c0 + c5\) (constant appears). Setting \(c5=0\) gives \(A c0\) (good), but then \(A^2c0/(A)=A c0\) requires \(c1=0\) and uses \(A\neq 0\); still okay on \(A>0\). However with \(c1=0\), the term is exactly \(A c0\) and no constant if \(c5=0\). Then choose \(c0=-0.232366...\) and set \(c6=0.395876...\), \(c3=0.526565...\), \(c4=0\). This actually **can** match on domain \(A>0\) (or \(A\ge0\) with removable singular at 0). So **17 matches** under relaxed domain excluding \(A=0\) (physically plausible if \(A>0\)).

### 18. Has \(c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(Ac7+c8)\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\) so \(e^{0}=1\). Also set cubic terms \(c0=c1=0\) and extra linear terms so their sum matches. Then match sine. Matches.

### 19. Adds \(c5\log(c6|A|+1)\)
To match GT, must remove log: set \(c5=0\). Also set \(A^2c0\) to 0. Then it becomes linear + sine with phase, so match as usual. Matches.

### 20. Has denominator \((A+c1)\) and logs
Can set log coefficient terms to 0, but still left with denominator-bearing linear/sine terms; no clean way to become exactly linear+sine without denominator for all \(A\). No match.

### 21. Has extra constant and \(e^{Ac8}\)
Set \(c7=0\) to remove exponential-in-\(A\). Set \(c6=0\). Set \(A^2\) absent already. Then reduce to (9) form and match. Matches.

### 22. Has \(\sin^2\) and constant \(c2\)
To get pure sine, must set \(c3=0\) (kills \(\sin^2\)), but then no sine remains. No match.

### 23–26. More complex rational/trig mixtures
All include extra rational factors or higher powers multiplying sine that cannot be removed while keeping exactly one plain sine plus one linear term, except by zeroing sine or leaving unwanted structure. No match for 23–26.

### 27. Has \(c5\sin(\cdot)\cos(c8 t)\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c8=0\) so \(\cos(0)=1\). Also set \(A^2c0=0\), set extra linear terms so sum matches, set constant \(c4=0\). Then match sine. Matches.

### 28. Has \(A c2 e^{c3 t}\) and \(c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(\cdot)\) plus constant
Set \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\) to remove \(t\). Set \(A^2c0=0\), set constant \(c4=0\). Then linear+sine remains and can match. Matches.

### 29. \(A^{c0}c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c2=0\). Make linear: set \(c0=1\). Then choose \(c1=-0.232366...\), \(c3=0.395876...\), \(c4=0.526565...\), \(c5=0\). Matches.

### 30. Adds \(t\)-dependent rational terms
Set \(c5=0\) and \(c7=0\) to remove those \(t\) terms. Then reduce to (3) and match. Matches.

### 31. Adds log of \(c6\exp(Ac7+c8 t)+1\)
To remove the log term, set its coefficient \(c5=0\). Then reduce to (3) and match. Matches.

### 32. Has \(A c1 e^{c2 t}\) and \(c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Set \(c2=0\) so \(e^{c2 t}=1\). Set \(c7\) irrelevant if \(c6=0\) to remove constant exponential term. Set \(A^2c0=0\). Then match linear+sine. Matches.

### 33–35. Denominators \((A+c1)\) or \((Ac1+c2)\) plus extra exponentials
Hard to eliminate denominators while keeping exact GT form; setting denominator-related coefficients to 0 removes needed linear structure, and remaining terms don’t match exactly. No match for 33–35.

### 36. \(A^2c0 + A c1/(Ac2+1) + c3\sin(\cdot) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
To match, need no \(A^2\): set \(c0=0\). Remove \(t\): set \(c6=0\). The term \(A c1/(Ac2+1)\) must become exactly linear \(-kA\); set \(c2=0\) so it becomes \(A c1\). Then choose \(c1=-0.232366...\) and match sine with \(c3=0.395876...\), etc. Matches.

### 37. Has extra constant \(c5\) and time-sine \(c6\sin(c7 t+c8)\)
Set \(c5=0\), \(c6=0\), \(A^2c0=0\). Then match remaining linear+sine. Matches.

### 38. Has rational-in-\(A\) linear terms and constant
Set \(c0=0\). To make \(A c2/(Ac3+1)\) linear, set \(c3=0\) giving \(A c2\). Similarly set \(c5=0\) giving \(A c4\). Set \(c9=0\). Then match linear sum and sine. Matches.

### 39. Denominator \((Ac1+1)\) with multiple terms
Can set \(c1=0\) so denominator is 1, then set \(A^3\) and \(A^2\) coefficients to 0, leaving \(A c6 + A c7\sin(\cdot)\) which is not GT (sine multiplied by \(A\)). If instead set \(c7=0\) to remove that, you lose sine. No match.

### 40. \(A^2c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sin(\cdot) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Set \(c0=0\), \(c6=0\). Make \(A^{c1}c2\) linear by \(c1=1\), \(c2=-0.232366...\). Match sine with \(c3=0.395876...\), etc. Matches.

### 41. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + Ac2 + c3 + c4\sin(c5|A|+c6)\)
Assume \(A\ge0\). Set \(c0=0\), \(c3=0\). Need \(c1+c2=-0.232366...\). Set \(c4=0.395876...\), \(c5=0.526565...\), \(c6=0\). Matches.

### 42–43. Denominator structures / extra \(A^{c5}\) sine with \(t\)
Not reducible cleanly to GT without leaving denominators or extra \(A\)-dependent prefactors on sine. No match.

### 44. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A c2/(Ac3+1) + c4 + c5\sin(c6|A|+c7)\)
Assume \(A\ge0\). Set \(c0=0\), \(c4=0\). Make rational term linear by \(c3=0\) so it becomes \(A c2\). Then choose \(c1+c2=-0.232366...\). Match sine with \(c5=0.395876...\), \(c6=0.526565...\), \(c7=0\). Matches.

### 45. Only polynomial/rational terms, no sine
Cannot match GT’s sine term. No match.

### 46. Has log term and sine with \(|A|\)
Assume \(A\ge0\). Set \(A^2c0=0\), set log coefficient \(c3=0\), set constant \(c2=0\). Then match linear and sine. Matches.

### 47. Has log term but no plain sine? (it has no sine)
Actually it has only log and rational linear terms, no sine. Cannot match. No match.

### 48. Sine of log(\(|A|\)) plus other terms
To get \(\sin(kA)\) you’d need the sine argument linear in \(A\), but it is \(\,c6\log(c7|A|+1)+c8\). Only way out is set \(c5=0\) (remove sine), but then no sine remains. No match.

### 49. Denominator terms plus \(e^{c8 t}\log(Ac9+1)\)
Even if log term set to 0, still denominator structure prevents exact GT without leftover rational dependence. No match.

### 50. Same issue as 48 (sine of log)
No match.

### 51. Has \(A^2\) term and \(e^{Ac8}\)
Set \(c0=0\), set \(c7=0\) (remove exponential), set \(c6=0\). Then reduce to linear+sine and match. Matches.

### 52. Has \(e^{Ac6}\) term
Set \(c5=0\) to remove exponential term; set \(A^2c0=0\). Then match linear+sine and set constant \(c7=0\). Matches.

### 53. Has denominator and \(A^{c5}\) multiplying sine
Hard to remove denominator while keeping correct linear term; also sine amplitude depends on \(A^{c5}\) unless \(c5=0\) (then amplitude constant), but denominator still remains in linear part. No match.

### 54–55. Include sine of log(...) plus extra terms
To match GT, would need sine argument linear in \(A\); it’s log-based. Setting sine coefficient to 0 removes sine entirely. No match.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT: -0.23236613283613416*A + 0.395876449251558*sin(0.5265654762365851*A)**

This is: `c_linear * A + c_sin * sin(c_freq * A)` — a linear term in A plus a sinusoidal term in A, with no constant offset, no dependence on t, no higher-order terms.

Let me analyze each candidate:

### Candidate 1: `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5)`
Set c0=0, then: A*(c1+c2) + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5). Set c5=0. This gives linear A + sin(A*c4). **MATCH**

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 2: `A*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2 + c3)² + c4`
sin² is not the same as sin. sin²(x) = (1-cos(2x))/2. This gives A*c0 + c1/2 - c1/2*cos(2*A*c2+2*c3) + c4. The GT has sin, not cos. These are linearly independent basis functions. **NO MATCH**

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`
Set c1=0, c4=0: A*c0 + c2*sin(A*c3). **MATCH**

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4: `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3*Abs(A) + c4)`
With domain A≥0, Abs(A)=A. Set c1=0, c4=0: A*c0 + c2*sin(c3*A). **MATCH**

Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 5: `A*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6`
Set c6=0, c5=0, combine linear terms. **MATCH**

Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 6: `A*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(c4*Abs(A) + c5)`
With A≥0, set c2=0, c5=0. **MATCH**

Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 7: `A^c0 * c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5`
Set c0=1, c5=0, c4=0: c1*A + c2*sin(A*c3). **MATCH**

### Candidate 8: `A*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`
